<div id="review_3085454387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3085454387" />
    <a title="Tyler Bell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38285760-tyler-bell"><img alt="Tyler Bell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605635745p2/38285760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3085454387?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tyler Bell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tyler Bell" href="/user/show/38285760-tyler-bell">Tyler Bell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/30811794-the-elementals">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3085454387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12338596159566479898"><i>
  <b>3.75/5 Stars</b>
</i><br/><br/><br/><b>A real interesting take on the <i>haunted house</i> story</b><br/><br/><br/>This book was written in 1981, and follws two families connected through marriage that go to their secluded summer homes in Alabama. Spooky things start to ensue when they arrive.<br/><br/>I've wanted to read this book for a while now. I decided to pick up the audiobook and I must say that the audiobook was surprisingly fantastic!<br/><br/>First, I'm going to start with the things that I didn't like. First and foremost, as I've stated in my reading u</span>
  <span id="freeText12338596159566479898" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>3.75/5 Stars</b>
</i><br /><br /><br /><b>A real interesting take on the <i>haunted house</i> story</b><br /><br /><br />This book was written in 1981, and follws two families connected through marriage that go to their secluded summer homes in Alabama. Spooky things start to ensue when they arrive.<br /><br />I've wanted to read this book for a while now. I decided to pick up the audiobook and I must say that the audiobook was surprisingly fantastic!<br /><br />First, I'm going to start with the things that I didn't like. First and foremost, as I've stated in my reading updates, Odessa Red is a character that I grew to love the most. She was such a mysterious characters and I wanted to know everything she knew. The things I didn't like about her character are mainly because of the author. The author introduced Odessa as the Savage family's housekeeper. With Odessa being black, this rubbed me the wrong way. However, I'm glad to have found out that the other characters that have employed Odessa regard her as a part of their own family, and don't really view her as a housekeeper, even though she still attends to her "duties". Odessa is actually regarded as the most respected and loved character in the entire book! Everyone takes her word for everything. But the other thing that annoyed me about the way Odessa was written was that the author kept having to repeat himself saying that she was a black woman. I found myself saying <i>"You don't need to keep repeating yourself. You don't describe every other character as being a 'white woman' or a 'white man', so why do you have to keep telling us that Odessa is in fact a black woman?"</i> I dunno, it just seemed so strange to me. <br /><br />The last thing that annoyed me about this book was the relationship that was between Luker and his daughter India. They seemed <i>waaaayy</i> too close to be father and daughter. It was so weird to me. And even the way that Luker talked to her was strange. Like, if I was India, I'd leave Luker behind becuase I'd be traumatized if my father talked to me like that on a daily basis. He would talk extensively about sex, drugs and call India names while having a smile on his face. He would also give India alcohol... AND SHE'S 13 YEARS OLD. I don't know if maybe this kind of relationship was common in the deep South, but it was severely unnerving to me.<br /><br />Other than those issues, this book has incredible characters. The way McDowell was able to incorporate so much characterization in such a small amout of time, and in a horror novel, was amazing to me. I feel like each character was fully realized and I was able to picture them easily. <br /><br />The plot was also really interesting! It was a bit of a different take on the hauted house trope and I really appreciate McDowell in setting this book apart from the others in this genre. He was able to give ample background information about the setting and characters that the events that happen to them seem real! He took his time in revealing things to us that it really made me want to keep reading. <br /><br />I said this in one of my reading updates that this book would make a great TV show or movie. The whole time that I was reading this I could pictre everything that was happening, and that's a sign of a good book. <br /><br />Overall, this book definitely has its issues, but it also has really incredible strengths. The scares are very well timed and genuinely sent a chill up my spine a few times. I recommend the audiobook because R.C. Bray is a great narrator!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12338596159566479898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3610442549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3610442549" />
    <a title="Beverly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly"><img alt="Beverly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505852430p2/68708752.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3610442549?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beverly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beverly" href="/user/show/68708752-beverly">Beverly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22461751-the-elementals">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3610442549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4586263124993023490">So truly wonderful and scary on many levels, The Elementals, is one of my favorite reads this year. What does it touch on? To name a few things it gets perfect are: a blunt, honest and loving relationship between a teenage daughter and her dad, southern mores and speech patterns done right, family dynamics, hot weather, and one mind-numbingly disturbing, malevolent house. <br/><br/>Beldame is the isolated retreat of the Savages and the McCrays. It consists of three, that's right three Victorian mansions s</span>
  <span id="freeText4586263124993023490" style="display:none">So truly wonderful and scary on many levels, The Elementals, is one of my favorite reads this year. What does it touch on? To name a few things it gets perfect are: a blunt, honest and loving relationship between a teenage daughter and her dad, southern mores and speech patterns done right, family dynamics, hot weather, and one mind-numbingly disturbing, malevolent house. <br /><br />Beldame is the isolated retreat of the Savages and the McCrays. It consists of three, that's right three Victorian mansions set next to the Alabama gulf, far away from everything. Marian Savage, the cruel, cold matriarch of the family has just passed and the families go to Beldame for the summer. The Savages still own one house and the McCrays, connected by friendship and family ties to the Savages, owns another. House Three is abandoned and has been inundated by sand which has broken into the house and almost covered it on one side.<br /><br />Written in 1981, The Elementals has as its main characters a thirteen year old girl raised in New York by her Alabama raised dad, and a middle-aged black woman who is the maid of the Savages and also their friend. India, the girl, and Odessa are not friends at first, but become linked by a sensitivity to the evil in the third house and fight to keep their loved ones safe. <br /><br />The portrayal of the girl is particularly good. She speaks her mind, without being a brat. She and her father cuss like sailors which her southern grandmother decries. India and Odessa are magnificent creations. The conversations that India has with her father are brilliant. On meeting her runaway mother on a New York street, Luker, the dad, yells, F... Off, B...ch! I love it. Anyway, this is scary and well written and I can't wait to read more from this author, who, left us early because of AIDS, that scourge of my youth, which still has no vaccine.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4586263124993023490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1396205568" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1396205568" />
    <a title="David Brian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16112063-david-brian"><img alt="David Brian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502287798p2/16112063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1396205568?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Brian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Brian" href="/user/show/16112063-david-brian">David Brian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1396205568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16329206067607519765">There are certain books which I tend to think of fondly and consider as favorites, only later to re-read and discover that the passing of time has dulled the enjoyment I felt during that initial reading. Maybe, in later years, I will re-read The Elementals by Michael McDowell, and perhaps by then I will have found more deserving favorites.<br/>It's a possibility.<br/>For now though, I would have to say that The Elementals is the finest example of Southern Gothic, and/or Quiet Horror, that I have had the p</span>
  <span id="freeText16329206067607519765" style="display:none">There are certain books which I tend to think of fondly and consider as favorites, only later to re-read and discover that the passing of time has dulled the enjoyment I felt during that initial reading. Maybe, in later years, I will re-read The Elementals by Michael McDowell, and perhaps by then I will have found more deserving favorites.<br />It's a possibility.<br />For now though, I would have to say that The Elementals is the finest example of Southern Gothic, and/or Quiet Horror, that I have had the pleasure of reading. And this book really was a pleasure, start to finish!<br /><br />The Elementals opens with the funeral of matriarch Marian Savage, where proceedings move forward at a fairly pedestrian pace; although the bizarre events surrounding the service are sure to pique the readers interest.<br /><br />Following the funeral service and internment, members of the Savage and McCray families set off for a period of reflection at their long-time seasonal holiday retreat of Beldame, an isolated spit of land that is set between The Gulf and St Elmo's Lagoon, and whereon stand three Victorian properties. At certain hours of the day when the tide is high, Beldame becomes an island. As well as the McCray and Savage homes, Beldame also hosts the mysterious Third House, a source of much consternation down the years among McCray and Savage children, who have long believed it houses something otherworldly. <br /><br />A motley assemblage of characters arrive at Beldame, including Luker McCray and his precocious thirteen year old daughter, India. To describe their relationship as having an unusual dynamic is an understatement. They drink together and cus like old soldiers, and it seems likely that India knows every aspect of her divorced father's life. But, much like every other main player in The Elementals, their characters are well drawn and their oft quirky natures only add to their overall appeal.<br /><br />Once at Beldame the book maintains its slow pace, and India strikes up a relationship with Odessa, the (other)worldly-wise maid. This was perhaps the only cliched part of the writing. Odessa repeatedly addresses India as "child," and the author continually refers to Odessa as "the black woman." But these were two minor irritations. For the most part, McDowell's prose is word perfect as he creates a visual of white-salt sands and the inescapable, overpowering heat of a Southern summer. I actually felt that the slow-burn of the book aided with creating the growing sense of unease and impending dread; occasional "odd" events become more frequent leading towards an excellently disturbing climax. I've described this as quiet horror, but make no mistake, the creep-you-out factor continues to climb until you'll begin to look over your shoulder just to check that nothing unpleasant is keeping you company.<br />This was a great book, but you probably won't want to read it while you're sitting on a beach; and certainly not if you are alone on the beach after dark!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16329206067607519765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1172674752" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1172674752" />
    <a title="Mindi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6157592-mindi"><img alt="Mindi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538422738p2/6157592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1172674752?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mindi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mindi" href="/user/show/6157592-mindi">Mindi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781941147177" href="/book/show/22295362-the-elementals">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1172674752" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2121803379905087762">I felt that while The Elementals was entertaining, essentially it was flawed, and so I was unable to give it a 3 star rating.<br/><br/>Michael McDowell wrote this novel in 1980 during the golden age of paperback horror fiction. Some very talented horror writers were churning out a large number of quality horror novels during this period in the 70's and 80's, and while most of those titles are now out of print, the ones I have managed to find have been exceptionally good. <br/><br/>Recently, Valancourt Books brought</span>
  <span id="freeText2121803379905087762" style="display:none">I felt that while The Elementals was entertaining, essentially it was flawed, and so I was unable to give it a 3 star rating.<br /><br />Michael McDowell wrote this novel in 1980 during the golden age of paperback horror fiction. Some very talented horror writers were churning out a large number of quality horror novels during this period in the 70's and 80's, and while most of those titles are now out of print, the ones I have managed to find have been exceptionally good. <br /><br />Recently, Valancourt Books brought a number of these works back into print, with new introductions by other horror writers who were originally inspired by these novels. I have really enjoyed a number of the obscure titles from that time, so when I read the synopsis of The Elementals I was sure I had found another title to add to my list of superb 70's and 80's horror fiction.<br /><br />I don't want to ruin too much of the plot here, but essentially there are supernatural forces in one of the three houses that make up Beldame, a plot of land on the Alabama Gulf Coast that is owned by two very close and wealthy families. Everyone is afraid of the third house, but for some reason nobody has a problem spending weeks at a time at Beldame, even though a number of people have died there, and there is obviously something wrong with the place.<br /><br />After the matriarch of one of the families passes away, the remaining relatives decided to spend time at the summer homes in order to regroup and deal with her death. Just don't go in the third house, and don't ask any questions.<br /><br />The novel is written mostly from the point of view of a wise beyond her years 13-year-old girl who has grown up in New York City, never having been to Alabama until the family funeral. She has an odd relationship with her father, who sees no point in shielding her from anything, but rather allows her to drink, curse, and even see him walking around in the nude at times. It's weird, and while I can appreciate a smart, fearless female protagonist, her reactions to everything around her just seem off for a girl her age.<br /><br />The novel also shows its age a bit by constantly referring to the maid employed by one of the families as black. We get it. The two families are wealthy white people with an African American maid. It's really not necessary to constantly refer to her as the "black woman" who, for some inexplicable reason, is the only person to actually see and understand the supernatural entities at Beldame.<br /><br />Sadly, there are just too many plot holes to allow me to rank this novel up there with some of my favorite horror stories. The Elementals themselves don't really make a lot of sense, and seem to have no rhyme or reason to their existence. At times, the maid Odessa seems to understand exactly what needs to be done to keep The Elementals at bay, and at others she doesn't have a clue. In the end the family endures even more tragedy because after a string of disturbing instances, nobody has the good sense to stay the hell away from Beldame. There are some genuinely creepy moments in the novel, but overall it just didn't work for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2121803379905087762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2093451048" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2093451048" />
    <a title="Ginny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8846320-ginny"><img alt="Ginny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440422835p2/8846320.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2093451048?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ginny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ginny" href="/user/show/8846320-ginny">Ginny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/33875079-the-elementals">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8846320-ginny?shelf=scary">scary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8846320-ginny?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2093451048" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2838078292029678939">I don't as a rule read horror books anymore, gore is boring and it's a genre overpopulated with silly plots. I was tempted into listening to this by it's promise of something more literary and subtle in nature, and it didn't disappoint. A highly satisfying mix of dry humour and creepiness, with great characters brought to life by the always superb R C Bray (I developed a real soft spot for Big Barbara, bless her, purely due to his wonderfully sympathetic portrayal). In his hands the atmospheric </span>
  <span id="freeText2838078292029678939" style="display:none">I don't as a rule read horror books anymore, gore is boring and it's a genre overpopulated with silly plots. I was tempted into listening to this by it's promise of something more literary and subtle in nature, and it didn't disappoint. A highly satisfying mix of dry humour and creepiness, with great characters brought to life by the always superb R C Bray (I developed a real soft spot for Big Barbara, bless her, purely due to his wonderfully sympathetic portrayal). In his hands the atmospheric heat and isolation of the setting provide the perfect accompaniment to the ever-present, sifting, creeping, watchful sands. <br /><br />I would read/listen to much more horror if it were of this standard...but NOT on the beach!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2838078292029678939" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P4z6+/5iWVxLr3ZN+RktT+6eJQ/IKVo3PJmCyMKILvY+GceKHdO+K4V9MYPJlLwX8AFGz5OnjA9iQQhmy6fovQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5818IP3dkif2d87L1ZSMqfR6qmnzGIPzh07ns1BzTZTmWEFRHmx1UDiliQXlGR3x6uXJqaiWVcvZlm0dWVyL3w==')})
  }

In her heart, Katherine had found God. In her father’s heart, they found a butcher knife.\n\nANDREA\n\nShe grew up with all that money could buy. She was pretty and popular and went to the best schools. Her parents loved her dearly, and gladly did anything to please her. But what made Andrea happy, would make them dead.\n\nTHEY MET IN THEIR NIGHTMARES\n\nIn the dark of sleep, Katherine and Andrea had terrible dreams of being the other. Until the hand of evil that guided their waking lives brought them face to face with each other . . . and the crossed fate of horror awaiting them both.\n\nReviews\n\n“Blood Rubies is an engrossing study of unconscious evil, unreflective evil, and it is the sign of the book’s wit and audacity that the evil figure is a nun . . .       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/90037.Michael_McDowell">About Michael McDowell</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/90037.Michael_McDowell"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1304622716p3/90037.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/90037.Michael_McDowell">Michael McDowell
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
578
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13127353162274633460">Michael McDowell is a prolific horror writer who has distinguished himself with a varied body of work within the genre. He was born in Enterprise, Alabama, in 1950 and died of AIDS-related illness in Boston, Massachusetts, in 1999.<br/><br/>His first horror novel, <i>The Amulet</i>, relates the tragedies that befall various individuals who come in possession of a supernatural pendant in a small town. <br/><br/>In McDowell's</span>
  <span id="freeText13127353162274633460" style="display:none">Michael McDowell is a prolific horror writer who has distinguished himself with a varied body of work within the genre. He was born in Enterprise, Alabama, in 1950 and died of AIDS-related illness in Boston, Massachusetts, in 1999.<br /><br />His first horror novel, <i>The Amulet</i>, relates the tragedies that befall various individuals who come in possession of a supernatural pendant in a small town. <br /><br />In McDowell's second novel, <i>Cold Moon Over Babylon</i>, a murdered woman's corpse is dispatched into a river, but her spirit roams the land, and in the evening hours it seeks revenge on her killer even as he plots the demise of her surviving relatives. <br /><br />Don D'Ammassa, writing in the <i>St. James Guide to Horror, Ghost &amp; Gothic Writers</i>, noted that McDowell's ability to maintain a sense of mundane normalcy against supernatural activity provides the novel with "a fine balance between reality and unreality," and he called <i>Cold Moon Over Babylon</i> "one of the best ghost stories ever written at novel length."<br /><br />A similarly disturbing tension between dull reality and the supernatural is produced in <i>The Elementals</i>, wherein a host of visitors come to stay at a secluded house occupied by embodiments of elemental forces. <br /><br />McDowell's <i>Katie</i>, meanwhile, concerns a clairvoyant serial killer whose powers of perception enable her to evade her trackers. The attractive but deranged heroine of this novel manages to conduct her murderous activities despite the awareness of her parents, who are content to derive financial gain from their daughter's crimes.<br /><br />Madness is central to McDowell's <i>Toplin</i>, which details the vile imaginings of a man who suffers from mental illness but nonetheless determines to conduct himself within society. D'Ammassa praised Toplin as "perhaps the best novel ever written from the point of view of a schizophrenic."<br /><br />Among McDowell's other writings is the six-part serial novel Blackwater, a chronicle of a southern family drawn to the supernatural. In addition, McDowell has also supplied the screenplays for various films, including director Tim Burton's horror comedy <i>Beetlejuice</i> and his animated production <i>The Nightmare Before Christmas</i>.<br /><br />Stephen King called McDowell one of the "finest writers of paperback originals in America today." Tabitha King was asked to complete McDowell's unfinished novel <i>Candles Burning</i>, which was published in 2006 to good reviews. Concerning his career, McDowell never tried to be something he wasn't. "I am a commercial writer and I'm proud of that", he said in the book <i>Faces of Fear</i> in 1985. "I am writing things to be put in the bookstore next month. I think it is a mistake to try to write for the ages."</span>
  <a data-text-id="13127353162274633460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
